{"type":"response.output_text.done","content_index":0,"item_id":"msg_0e2ed64344ac7f31016994b30597248197afefe0ff4bfd83ec","logprobs":[],"output_index":0,"sequence_number":819,"text":"### Testing strategies: unit vs integration vs E2E (end-to-end)\n\nAll three test types answer different questions, run at different “distances” from your code, and trade off speed vs realism.\n\n---\n\n## 1) Unit tests (Jest)\n**What they test:** A *single unit* of code in isolation—typically a function, class method, reducer, utility, or component logic.\n\n**Goal:** Verify internal logic is correct independent of other systems.\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- **Fastest** (runs in milliseconds)\n- Lots of **mocking/stubbing** (mock network calls, databases, timers, etc.)\n- Failures are usually easy to pinpoint\n\n**Examples (from your guide):**\n- `describe`, `test`, `expect`\n- Matchers like `toBe`, `toEqual`\n\n**Typical use:**\n- Validate a price calculation function\n- Test a Redux reducer given an action\n- Test input validation helpers\n\n---\n\n## 2) Integration tests (Supertest)\n**What they test:** Multiple units working together—commonly your **API layer + middleware + routing + (sometimes) database**.\n\n**Goal:** Confirm that “wiring” between modules is correct (routing, serialization, auth middleware, validation, error handling).\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- **Slower than unit tests**, but still usually quick enough for CI\n- Uses fewer mocks; often uses a real HTTP server instance in-memory\n- You can choose the scope:\n  - **Shallow integration**: API routes + controllers, DB mocked\n  - **Full integration**: real DB (often a test DB/container), real middleware\n\n**Examples (from your guide):**\n- `supertest(app).get('/endpoint')...expect(200)`\n- `post`, `send`, `expect` status codes + response bodies\n\n**Typical use:**\n- Test `POST /api/users` returns `201` and the JSON schema you expect\n- Ensure auth middleware rejects missing/invalid JWT (`401`)\n- Confirm validation returns `422` with correct error payload\n\n---\n\n## 3) End-to-End (E2E) tests (Playwright)\n**What they test:** The full system from the user’s perspective: **real browser + frontend + backend + database** (as close to production as practical).\n\n**Goal:** Verify critical user journeys actually work (regressions that unit/integration tests might miss).\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- **Slowest and most brittle** (UI selectors, timing, environment)\n- Minimal mocking; you want realism\n- Best for a smaller number of high-value flows\n\n**Examples (from your guide):**\n- `page.goto(...)`\n- `page.fill(...)`, `page.click(...)`\n- Assertions on URL, title, and visible content\n\n**Typical use:**\n- “User can sign up, log in, and see dashboard”\n- “Add item to cart → checkout → confirmation”\n- “Form validation messages appear correctly in UI”\n\n---\n\n## How they differ (quick comparison)\n\n| Type | Scope | Runs where | Speed | Best for |\n|------|-------|------------|-------|----------|\n| Unit (Jest) | Single function/module | Node/test runner | Very fast | Logic correctness, edge cases |\n| Integration (Supertest) | Multiple modules + API surface | Node + HTTP layer | Medium | API behavior, middleware, routing |\n| E2E (Playwright) | Entire app | Real browser + real services | Slow | User journeys, regression coverage |\n\n---\n\n## Practical rule of thumb\n- Write **many unit tests** (broad coverage, cheap to run).\n- Add **integration tests** for your API boundaries and important module interactions.\n- Keep **E2E tests** focused on a handful of mission-critical flows.\n\nIf you tell me your stack (React/Vue + Node/Express + DB) and what you’re building, I can suggest a balanced test pyramid and a minimal set of E2E flows."}

you want realism\n- Best for a smaller number of high-value flows\n\n**Examples (from your guide):**\n- `page.goto(...)`\n- `page.fill(...)`, `page.click(...)`\n- Assertions on URL, title, and visible content\n\n**Typical use:**\n- “User can sign up, log in, and see dashboard”\n- “Add item to cart → checkout → confirmation”\n- “Form validation messages appear correctly in UI”\n\n---\n\n## How they differ (quick comparison)\n\n| Type | Scope | Runs where | Speed | Best for |\n|------|-------|------------|-------|----------|\n| Unit (Jest) | Single function/module | Node/test runner | Very fast | Logic correctness, edge cases |\n| Integration (Supertest) | Multiple modules + API surface | Node + HTTP layer | Medium | API behavior, middleware, routing |\n| E2E (Playwright) | Entire app | Real browser + real services | Slow | User journeys, regression coverage |\n\n---\n\n## Practical rule of thumb\n- Write **many unit tests** (broad coverage, cheap to run).\n- Add **integration tests** for your API boundaries and important module interactions.\n- Keep **E2E tests** focused on a handful of mission-critical flows.\n\nIf you tell me your stack (React/Vue + Node/Express + DB) and what you’re building, I can suggest a balanced test pyramid and a minimal set of E2E flows."},"sequence_number":820}

Testing strategies: unit vs integration vs E2E (end-to-end)\n\nAll three test types answer different questions, run at different “distances” from your code, and trade off speed vs realism.\n\n---\n\n## 1) Unit tests (Jest)\n**What they test:** A *single unit* of code in isolation—typically a function, class method, reducer, utility, or component logic.\n\n**Goal:** Verify internal logic is correct independent of other systems.\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- **Fastest** (runs in milliseconds)\n- Lots of **mocking/stubbing** (mock network calls, databases, timers, etc.)\n- Failures are usually easy to pinpoint\n\n**Examples (from your guide):**\n- `describe`, `test`, `expect`\n- Matchers like `toBe`, `toEqual`\n\n**Typical use:**\n- Validate a price calculation function\n- Test a Redux reducer given an action\n- Test input validation helpers\n\n---\n\n## 2) Integration tests (Supertest)\n**What they test:** Multiple units working together—commonly your **API layer + middleware + routing + (sometimes) database**.\n\n**Goal:** Confirm that “wiring” between modules is correct (routing, serialization, auth middleware, validation, error handling).\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- **Slower than unit tests**, but still usually quick enough for CI\n- Uses fewer mocks; often uses a real HTTP server instance in-memory\n- You can choose the scope:\n  - **Shallow integration**: API routes + controllers, DB mocked\n  - **Full integration**: real DB (often a test DB/container), real middleware\n\n**Examples (from your guide):**\n- `supertest(app).get('/endpoint')...expect(200)`\n- `post`, `send`, `expect` status codes + response bodies\n\n**Typical use:**\n- Test `POST /api/users` returns `201` and the JSON schema you expect\n- Ensure auth middleware rejects missing/invalid JWT (`401`)\n- Confirm validation returns `422` with correct error payload\n\n---\n\n## 3) End-to-End (E2E) tests (Playwright)\n**What they test:** The full system from the user’s perspective: **real browser + frontend + backend + database** (as close to production as practical).\n\n**Goal:** Verify critical user journeys actually work (regressions that unit/integration tests might miss).\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- **Slowest and most brittle** (UI selectors, timing, environment)\n- Minimal mocking; you want realism\n- Best for a smaller number of high-value flows\n\n**Examples (from your guide):**\n- `page.goto(...)`\n- `page.fill(...)`, `page.click(...)`\n- Assertions on URL, title, and visible content\n\n**Typical use:**\n- “User can sign up, log in, and see dashboard”\n- “Add item to cart → checkout → confirmation”\n- “Form validation messages appear correctly in UI”\n\n---\n\n## How they differ (quick comparison)\n\n| Type | Scope | Runs where | Speed | Best for |\n|------|-------|------------|-------|----------|\n| Unit (Jest) | Single function/module | Node/test runner | Very fast | Logic correctness, edge cases |\n| Integration (Supertest) | Multiple modules + API surface | Node + HTTP layer | Medium | API behavior, middleware, routing |\n| E2E (Playwright) | Entire app | Real browser + real services | Slow | User journeys, regression coverage |\n\n---\n\n## Practical rule of thumb\n- Write **many unit tests** (broad coverage, cheap to run).\n- Add **integration tests** for your API boundaries and
